Liselotte Grschebina is a modern Hebrew poet, writer, and translator. Her first book of poetry, "Of Love and Sorrow", was published in 1984. Her poems have appeared in literary journals and anthologies in Israel, France, Germany, and the United States. She is also the author of several books of prose, including "The House of the Tribe of Benjamin" and "The Merchant of the World." She has received several prizes and awards for her work. In addition to her native Hebrew, Grschebina writes in German, Russian, and English. She lives in Berlin.  Liselotte Grschebina was born in Karlsruhe, Germany, in 1947. She received her education at the School of Applied Arts in Stuttgart. She is a citizen of Israel and lives in Berlin.  Karlsruhe is a city in southwestern Germany. It is the capital of the state of Baden-Württemberg and is the fourth-largest city in Germany. It lies on the Rhine River, which flows from Lake Constance into the Rhine-Main-Danube Canal. Karlsruhe is the seat of the German Federal Constitutional Court and the Karlsruhe Court of Appeals. ''' The Fellowship of the Ring is a 1954 epic fantasy novel by English writer J. R. R. Tolkien. It is the first volume of The Lord of the Rings trilogy, and was published in the United Kingdom on 21 September 1954. The novel follows the journey of a company of hobbits led by the wizard Gandalf, on their quest to destroy the One Ring of Power and its bearer, the Dark Lord Sauron, and thus prevent the latter's domination of Middle-earth. The Fellowship of the Ring won the 1955 Hugo Award for Best Novel, and was a runner-up for the 1954 Nebula Award for Best Novel. It has been adapted for film twice, first in the UK in 1978, and again in the United States in 2001. The novel is often considered the greatest work of English-language fantasy of the 20th century, and one of the greatest novels of all time. In 1999, it was voted the best book of the 20th century in a poll of book critics by the BBC, and in 2003 was placed second on a similar poll conducted by the Guardian newspaper. In a survey of the 100 greatest novels ever written, the BBC named it the best novel of the 20th century, and the Guardian placed it at number four. In 2012, it was named the second best book of the 20th century in a BBC poll of 100 writers, editors, and critics. The Fellowship of the Ring is set in the fictional universe of Middle-earth, which Tolkien created and developed over a period of more than fifty years. The novel was written during World War II, and follows the hobbits Frodo Baggins and Samwise Gamgee as they make their way towards Mount Doom, where the One Ring of Power is destroyed. Frodo is the bearer of the One Ring, which has been passed down through the generations of his family. The book begins with the Fellowship's departure from Rivendell, where the elves had guarded the Ring for many years. The Fellowship is joined by the wizard Gandalf, and they pass through the Misty Mountains, where they are attacked by trolls. After crossing the Misty Mountains, they reach Bree, where they are ambushed by the spider Shelob, and then continue on to Rivendell. Frodo and Sam are then taken to the Elvenking Elrond, who forbids them from proceeding towards Mord

'''  import nltk import re  class FluentText:      def init(self, inputstring):         self.inputstring = inputstring         self.outputstring = ''      def convert(self):         self.triplelist = []         self.triplelist.extend(self.convertrelationships())         self.triplelist.extend(self.convertbirthdeathplaces())         self.outputstring = ''.join(self.triplelist)      def convertrelationships(self):         rematches = re.findall(r'(\w+)\.\ \w+\ \w+ spouse \w+', self.inputstring)         for rematch in rematches:             self.outputstring += '%s spouse %s\n' % (rematch[0], rematch[1])         return self.outputstring      def convertbirthdeathplaces(self):         rematches = re.findall(r'(\w+)\.\ \w+\ \w+ birthPlace (\w+)', self.inputstring)         for rematch in rematches:             self.outputstring += '%s birthPlace %s\n' % (rematch[0], rematch[1])         rematches = re.findall(r'(\w+)\.\ \w+\ \w+ deathPlace (\w+)', self.inputstring)         for rematch in rematches:             self.outputstring += '%s deathPlace %s\n' % (rematch[0], rematch[1])         return self.outputstring  def main():     text = 'AbrahamA.Ribicoff spouse CaseyRibicoff\nAbrahamA.Ribicoff deathPlace UnitedStates\nAbrahamA.Ribicoff birthPlace UnitedStates'     f = FluentText(text)     f.convert()     print f.outputstring  if name == 'main':     main()

Yr Dref Ffwrnog Alaw is a city in the Mexican state of Morelos. It is located in the south of the state, in the municipal seat of Cuernavaca. The population of the city is estimated at about 35,000 inhabitants. The city is named after the first president of Mexico, Guadalupe Victoria, who was born in the town of Padilla, Tamaulipas, in northwestern Mexico. The city was founded in November 17, 1660, by the Spanish Governor of the province of New Spain, Martín de Mayorga. The city was founded as a military outpost to protect the borders of the province from attacks by the Chichimeca Indians. In the mid-18th century, the city was abandoned, and it was not until the mid-20th century that it was once again inhabited. It was then that the city began to grow and develop, with the construction of the Palacio de Cortés, the Teatro Ocampo, the Plaza de Armas, the Palacio de Gobierno, the Teatro de la Paz, the Palacio Federal, and the Cathedral de Cuernavaca. In the early 21st century, the city has become a major tourist destination, with a large number of hotels and restaurants, and a large number of residents who are employed in the tourism sector. The city is located in the center of the state, about 100 kilometers from Mexico City, and it is also the capital of the municipality of the same name. The city is the seat of the Cuernavaca Cathedral, the seat of the Diocese of Cuernavaca, which covers the state of Morelos and the southern part of the state of Mexico. The city is served by the Cuernavaca International Airport, which is located in the municipality of Emiliano Zapata, about 5 kilometers from the city center. The city is also the site of the Morelos Museum, which is located in the center of the city, and contains a large collection of artifacts from the colonial period, as well as several paintings by famous artists. The city is also the site of the Cuernavaca Botanical Garden, which is located about 10 kilometers from the city center. The city is also the site of the Cuernavaca Convention Center, which is located in the north of the city, and contains a large number of exhibitions of works of art. Eglwys Bach  Eglwys Bach is a village in the Vale of Glamorgan, Wales. It is located 3 miles south of Barry, 3 miles north of the town of Cadoxton and 2 miles west of the town of Penarth. It is the location of Barry Island railway station, which serves Barry Island, and the village of Barry.  Eglwys Bach is situated in the Vale of Glamorgan. The village is part of the Barry Rural community. The village has a population of around 200 people, with most of the population working in the nearby town of Barry. The village has a small number of businesses and is home to the Vale of Glamorgan Council's Barry Island Leisure Centre.  The village is named after the church which was built in the 15th century. The village is also known as the home of the Penarth Pier and is close to the Cardiff Bay area.  The village is served by Barry Island railway station, which is on the Vale of Glamorgan Line. The railway line runs through the village and the station was built in 1864. It was originally a horse drawn station but was converted to a railway station in the 20th century. The station is also home to the Barry Island Tramway, which runs from the station to Barry Island. The tramway was built in the 19th century and is now a tourist attraction.  The village has a primary school, which was built in the 19th century. It is also home to the Barry Island Golf Club, which was built in the 19th century.  The village is home to Barry Island Sailing Club, which is located on the pier. The club was founded in the 19th century and is home to the Barry Island Regatta, which is an annual event. YstradCynwyd, October 1, 2014 (GLOBE NEWSWIRE) -- SuperCapers, Inc. (OTCQB: SCPA) is pleased to announce that its board of directors has appointed RayGriggs as its new CEO and director. Griggs, who has over 20 years of business experience, will oversee the company's business operations and will work with the board of directors to develop strategies for the company's growth. Griggs is a retired Army captain and has been an entrepreneur and business executive for over 20 years. He was the founder of a leading Internet security company, RayGriggsSecurity, which was sold to a Fortune 100 company. Griggs has also been involved with several other technology companies. He currently serves as the CEO and director of the company. "I'm excited to be a part of the SuperCapers team," Griggs said. "I am looking forward to working with the board of directors to help the company reach its full potential." SuperCapers, Inc. is a technology company that focuses on developing and marketing its patented technology for the generation of electricity from waste heat. The company's patented technology is designed to generate electricity from waste heat generated by any hot process, including industrial processes, commercial buildings and residential buildings. The technology is designed to generate electricity from a variety of waste heat sources, including the heat from combustion engines, the heat from turbines and the heat from the exhaust of jet engines. The company has a number of patents pending for the technology, which is designed to be cost effective and easy to install. The company is currently engaged in the development of its first product, a heat to power generator, which will be used to generate electricity from the waste heat from a jet engine. Darinka Dentcheva (born 1958) is a Bulgarian mathematician who is known for her work on stochastic programming.  She is currently a professor of mathematical optimization at the Department of Mathematics of the University of Texas at Austin.  Dentcheva graduated from the Sofia University in 1978, and earned her PhD from the same institution in 1982. She was an assistant professor at the Bulgarian Academy of Sciences from 1982 to 1986, and an associate professor at the University of Minnesota from 1986 to 1993. In 1993, she became a full professor at the University of Texas at Austin.  Dentcheva is a fellow of the Institute of Mathematical Statistics, a fellow of the Institute of Operations Research and Management Science, and a fellow of the Society for Industrial and Applied Mathematics.  Dentcheva was awarded the first prize at the International Mathematical Olympiad in 1976. She was awarded the John von Neumann Theory Prize in 2000, the 2003 Gödel Prize, and the 2008 Leroy P. Steele Prize.  She has been a consultant to the World Bank, the Asian Development Bank, and the United Nations.  References  B. Dantzig, G. Fulkerson, and D. P. Wolfe, "Linear programming and extensions", Princeton University Press, Princeton, New Jersey, 1963.  D. Dentcheva, "Optimal stochastic control of production processes", Stochastic Processes and their Applications, 2(3), 1986.  D. Dentcheva and A. Ruszczyński, "A comparison of various approaches to the analysis of production systems with random yields", Operations Research Letters, 10(1), 1991.  D. Dentcheva and S. Ruszczyński, "Stochastic production planning with uncertain yields", Mathematical Programming, 58(1), 1992.  D. Dentcheva, "Control of production systems with random yields", PhD thesis, University of Minnesota, 1993.  D. Dentcheva and J. Zhang, "Stochastic production planning with yield uncertainty", Operations Research, 50(6), 2002.  D. Dentcheva, S. Ruszczyński, and J. Zhang, "Stochastic production planning with yield uncertainty and learning effects", European Journal of Operational Research, 157(2), 2004.  D. Dentcheva and J. Zhang, "Stochastic production planning with yield uncertainty, learning effects and machine breakdowns", European Journal of Operational Research, 160(3), 2005

Yr Ynys Prydain (Year of No Light) was a Welsh rock band formed in 1979 by members of the band Aphrodite's Child. Their sound was heavily influenced by progressive rock. The band recorded only one album, titled Yr Ynys Prydain (Year of No Light), before disbanding in 1982.

Darinka Dentcheva is a mathematician specializing in mathematical optimization. She is a professor of mathematics at the University of Wisconsin–Madison. She received her Ph.D. from the University of California, Berkeley in 1986. Her research focuses on optimization, in particular on algorithms for solving optimization problems, and on applications in economics and finance. She is known for her work on interior point methods and for her work on mathematical economics. She is a member of the National Academy of Sciences.
Alan B. Miller Hall was designed by Robert A. M. Stern, who is also the architect of the nearby Williamsburg Savings Bank and the National Museum of American Jewish History. It is home to the Mason School of Business of the College of William and Mary. The building is located in Williamsburg, Virginia.

Darinka Dentcheva (born 1958) is a Bulgarian mathematician, specializing in stochastic programming and mathematical optimization. She is currently a professor of mathematics at the Humboldt University of Berlin, Germany.  Dentcheva graduated from the Sofia University in 1982 with a degree in mathematics and earned her PhD from the same institution in 1986. She did her postdoctoral studies at the University of California, Berkeley, from 1987 to 1988. From 1988 to 1991, she was an assistant professor at the University of Michigan, Ann Arbor. She was a visiting professor at the University of Waterloo from 1991 to 1993 and at the University of California, Berkeley, from 1993 to 1995. She was promoted to a full professor in 1995.  Her research interests are in the areas of stochastic programming and mathematical optimization. She has published more than 50 papers in the area of stochastic programming, and has developed the Dentcheva–Rockafellar theorem, which relates the duality of a pair of primal–dual stochastic programs with the duality of a pair of linear programs. She has also developed a general duality theory for stochastic programs with recourse, and a general theory for the asymptotic behavior of discrete-time Markov decision processes. She is a Fellow of the Institute of Mathematical Statistics.  She is a member of the editorial boards of several mathematical journals. In 2011 she was elected a Fellow of the American Mathematical Society. She was elected to the National Academy of Sciences in Bulgaria in 2015. In 2018 she was elected a Foreign Member of the Royal Society.

Petah Tikva, meaning "Opening of Hope", is a city in Israel. It is the third most populous city in Israel, with a population of about 200,000.  Petah Tikva is located on the Sharon Plain, and is surrounded by the Jerusalem Hills to the south, the Judean Hills to the north, the Mediterranean Sea to the west, and the Sharon Plain to the east. The city is a center for the agriculture and food industry. Petah Tikva is also home to many industrial parks, and is the location of the Israeli Space Agency. Petah Tikva is the site of the annual Hebrew Song Festival.

Darinka Dentcheva is an associate professor at the Humboldt University of Berlin. She studied mathematics and computer science at the University of Sofia, where she received her PhD in 2008. Her research interests include the complexity of constraint satisfaction problems, in particular the computational complexity of Boolean functions and the complexity of reasoning about quantified Boolean formulas.  Darinka Dentcheva is the daughter of the Bulgarian mathematician Dimitar Dentchev. She is married to the mathematician Dimiter Tzvetkov, also from Bulgaria.

Buzz Aldrin gwas an American astronaut and the second person to step onto the Moon. He was a pilot of the lunar module Eagle during the Apollo 11 mission, which landed on July 20, 1969. He was the first person to step onto the lunar surface six hours after the landing. Aldrin is one of only twelve people to have flown in space twice, and only the second person, after Gennady Padalka, to have flown in space three times. In 2012, Time magazine named Aldrin as one of the 100 most influential people of the 20th century.

Brazil's leader, Vice President Michel Temer, has resigned, triggering a constitutional crisis that could bring the world's seventh-largest economy to its knees. The move comes less than two months after Dilma Rousseff was suspended from office on charges of breaking budget laws and on the eve of a vote that would have toppled her. The Senate voted by 55 to 22 to start impeachment proceedings against Ms Rousseff, and by 55 to 22 to suspend her from office for up to 180 days. The Senate's action was triggered by a request from the Chamber of Deputies, the lower house of Congress, which has a majority of lawmakers who support impeachment. The process will now continue in the Senate, which will vote on whether to remove Ms Rousseff from office. If the Senate votes to remove her, Vice President Michel Temer will assume the presidency until the end of the 2018 presidential term. The Senate has a maximum of 180 days to complete the process, and Mr Temer is expected to remain in office until then. Mr Temer, 75, is a former constitutionalist who was an ally of Ms Rousseff's Workers' Party before joining forces with a group of dissident lawmakers to push for her impeachment. He has vowed to push through austerity measures to restore confidence in Brazil's economy, which is in its worst recession in decades. Mr Temer is also accused of being involved in a corruption scandal that has engulfed the Workers' Party. In a statement, he said he would work to restore the confidence of the people of Brazil and the country's international partners. "It is time to restore the country's economic stability," he said. "We will be able to overcome the crisis and move towards the future with confidence." Ms Rousseff has said she will take legal action to overturn the Senate's decision, which she said was based on "false accusations". She has also accused Mr Temer of trying to take power in a coup. In a letter to Congress, Ms Rousseff said she was taking action to protect Brazil from what she called a "grave threat" to democracy. "It's not a time for resignation, it's a time for resistance," she wrote. She said she would be going to the Brazilian Supreme Court to contest the Senate's decision. Brazil's main stock market rose more than 3 per cent after the Senate voted to start the impeachment process. Ystad has a population of 4,500 and is the largest town in the municipality of Södermanland. Ystad is located in the south of Sweden, and is a part of the Stockholm metropolitan area. The town is situated on the banks of the river Säveån and is connected to the Swedish motorway network by the E20, E4 and E6 highways. Ystad is the main center of the Södermanland region and is the administrative center of the municipality. Ystad has a long history dating back to the 14th century, when the town was established as a trading port. Today, Ystad is a tourist destination and is known for its historic buildings and museums. In the town center, there are several old buildings, including the city hall and the church of St. Peter. The town also has several museums, including the Museum of Ystad and the Ystad Art Museum. Ystad is also home to the Swedish national archives and several libraries. Ystad has a growing business sector, with companies such as Volvo, Electrolux and Ericsson having their Swedish headquarters in the town. Ystad is also home to the Swedish Defense Materiel Administration, which is responsible for the Swedish defense industry. The town has a number of hotels, and is a popular tourist destination. Ystad is also home to several sports clubs, including the football club Ystads IF and the ice hockey club Ystads Hockey. Ystad is also home to the Södermanlands högskola, a teacher's college. Ystad was granted the status of town in 1543, and in 1771, the town became the seat of the bishopric of Ystad. In 1918, Ystad became a part of the newly formed county of Södermanland. In 1921, the name of the town was changed to Ystad after the river Säveån, which flows through the town.

Ystrad Mynach, an unincorporated community and a village in the county of Gwynedd, north Wales. It is situated near the village of Ystrad Tywi, to the south of the village of Dolwyddelan and to the north of the village of Penrhyndeudraeth. It is located near the town of Caernarfon, on the A4055 road, north of the River Dwyryd. It is home to the University of Wales Institute, Aberystwyth, which is situated on the site of the former Royal Air Force Station RAF Ystrad Mynach, the village's largest employer. The village is also the home of the Ystrad Mynach RFC, a rugby union team which plays in the Welsh Premier Division. The village has a population of about 2,000 and is served by a small community shop, the Ystrad Mynach Community Centre and a primary school. The village is also the home of the Ystrad Mynach War Memorial, which was unveiled on 14 July 1927. The village is also the home of the Ystrad Mynach Hall, which was built in 1888 as a town hall, and now serves as a venue for many local community events. Darinka Dentcheva (en serbiu: Дарінка Денчеве) je matematike i ekonomistka iz Serbia. Je graduirao iz Kragujevac, po svim studijama u Kragujevac, Kragujevac, u Niziji, i u Zagrebu. Od 1994. do 2004. godine je bila rektorica Ekonomskog fakulteta u Kragujevcu. Od 2004. do 2010. godine je bila rektorica Ekonomskog fakulteta u Zagrebu. Od 2010. do 2012. godine je bila rektorica Ekonomskog fakulteta u Niziji. Od 2012. do 2016. godine je bila rektorica Ekonomskog fakulteta u Kragujevcu. Od 2016. do 2018. godine je bila rektorica Ekonomskog fakulteta u Zagrebu. Od 2018. do 2020. godine je bila rektorica Ekonomskog fakulteta u Niziji. Od 2020. do 2022. godine je bila rektorica Ekonomskog fakulteta u Kragujevcu. Od 2022. do 2024. godine je bila rektorica Ekonomskog fakulteta u Zagrebu.  Darinka Dentcheva je bila obučena u priznanstvu iz Kragujevca (2003), Nizije (2004), Kragujevca (2005), Nizije (2006), Kragujevca (2007), Nizije (2008), Kragujevca (2009), Nizije (2010), Kragujevca (2011), Nizije (2012), Kragujevca (2013), Nizije (2014), Kragujevca (2015), Nizije (2016), Kragujevca (2017), Nizije (2018), Kragujevca (2019), Nizije (2020), Kragujevca (2021), Nizije (2022), Kragujevca (2023), Nizije (2024). U svrhu stvaranja i razvoja ekonomske nauke i ekonomskih i društvenih znanosti, je bila na članstvu u međunarodnim naučnim konferencijama,
